    \theutterance \stepcounter{utterance}  
    & \multicolumn{4}{p{0.6\linewidth}}{
        \cellcolor[rgb]{0.9,0.9,0.9}{
            \makecell[{{p{\linewidth}}}]{
                \texttt{\tiny{[P1$\rangle$GM]}}
                \texttt{The user asks: "Does the questioner know what is at the center? Answer this question with yes or no and then stop."} \\
\\ 
\texttt{I need to respond with: ASIDE: <one sentence>} \\
\\ 
\texttt{The instruction says: "Answer this question with yes or no and then stop."} \\
\\ 
\texttt{So I should give a one{-}sentence answer that is just "yes" or "no". The format is ASIDE: <one sentence>.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{The question is about whether the questioner knows what is at the center. Let me think about the situation.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{The initial description says: "Things are in different places, but the questioner does not know about it yet. Here is the situation:"} \\
\\ 
\texttt{This implies that the questioner doesn't know the locations yet. The questioner has been asking questions about where things are. They haven't asked about the center yet. So they don't know what's at the center.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Therefore, the answer is "no".} \\
\\ 
\texttt{I should format it as: ASIDE: no} \\
\\ 
\texttt{But wait, it says "Answer this question with yes or no and then stop." And "Please answer these questions with: ASIDE: <one sentence>".} \\
\\ 
\texttt{So a single word "no" is a sentence fragment, but it's the direct answer requested. I think "ASIDE: no" is appropriate following the instructions.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Let me double{-}check: The questioner has asked about southwest, right, bottom, top, southeast, here, northwest, left, inside {-} but not about center. So they don't know what's at the center.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{The answer is "no". I should just give that.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{ASIDE: no} \\
\\ 
\texttt{That's one sentence? Well, it's one word, but it's the answer format requested. The instruction says "Answer this question with yes or no and then stop." So I should just say "no" and nothing else.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{The format is ASIDE: <one sentence>. So "no" can be considered a one{-}word sentence.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Yes, I'll go with that. ASIDE: no} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Wait, let me re{-}read the ME question: "Does the questioner know what is at the center? Answer this question with yes or no and then stop."} \\
\\ 
\texttt{This is a meta{-}question about the questioner's knowledge state. The initial setup says "the questioner does not know about it yet" {-} meaning they don't know where things are. They've been asking questions to find out. So far, they haven't asked about the center. Therefore, they don't know what's at the center.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{So the answer is "no".} \\
\\ 
\texttt{And I need to follow the format: ASIDE: <one sentence>} \\
\\ 
\texttt{So: ASIDE: no} \\
\\ 
\texttt{That seems correct. It's short and direct as requested. ASIDE: no} \\
            }
        }
